1970
1. Birs. Vicioria FERNANDEZ Padiin, newly provided Attache at the
CHUS, was the subject of a naph passed to your office 2:
January 1970. Source "JAGIN" provided the following information
on FERNANDEZ on 1 February 1970.
2. FERNANDEZ will stay in New York City for probably about a
three month period; while here she will be working on documents
and files at the CHUN. In Havana, she is employed in the
document's section of the International Organizations
and the National Bureau of Statistics, and the above here
for three months for the same purpose in Pall 1969 during the
XXIV UN General Assembly, but Cuban Permanent Representation
ALAMCOH had objected so her travel was postponed. FERNANDEZ
is belleted in the apartment (5 N, 220 past Gaid Stroce)
and the 1969 conference was held in the 1969 conference. Attache;
GELABZET is staying temporarily with Regicio RODRIGUZ Lopez,
First Secretary, in his apartment in Queens, 15 M, 63-15 57th
street, Elnhurst. Neither GELABZET nor RODRIGUZ is happy over
this turn of events. FERNANDEZ is married, but Source does
not be made.
3. FERNANDEZ is fat and wry; she does not dress voll. She is
a mulato. She is not known for her intelligence quotient.
She has a somewhat rigid personality and does not get along
well with people, male or female. She is convinced that she
is discriminated against because she is part nero. FERNANDEZ
is
not
a
sociative
and
the
understand politics and ideologies. She takes herself extremely
seriously. Within MINNESZ she is a "loner"; older than most
of her female professional associates, she has nothing in
common with them and lice overbearing intitude is offensive to
them. Source believes that it is about a foreign conclusion
that FERNANDEZ and government Representative AIAKCON will have a
single choice for the next year.
4. FERNANDEZ' brother, Oscar FERNANDEZ Dailin, is Vice-Minister
for Labor Justice, Ministiey of Inbor. He is an "old gamed"
Communist, and Victoria FERNANDEZ is thus linked in some minds
to the out-of-favor old guard herself.
5. In previous years Victoria FERNANDEZ has served as an instructress
in the civil defense program. She has enjoyed being in a
position of authority over those normally, outside the training
program, her superiors in position and ability.
6. She has no known intelligence/security affiliations, but
Source believes that she would be happy to collaborate with
the DGI or DSE if so requested.

While ostensibly an andent revolutionary, BALLESTER
does not really understand revolution and appears to be
confused. Among other things, she is disturbed by the

concern of the United States, the American Society have
any contact with her at this time because she fears the

aid group. BALLESTER and MATTEL said this wealthy, by

TIPIC 100005 ANIOSE - Depicting of
Cuba IN Sission and Deregation Personalities
Action Required: Extract for appropriate 201 files
Rees: a. UNDA-1675, 14 October 1969
b. UNDA-1676, 14 October 1969
1: Attached herewith for C/WH/COG and COS/WH/NIAMI
are two copies each of three memorandu concerning results
of an 11 October 1969 debriefing of AMCLOCK/1 by Howard G.
FIGALAN on COUN and Delegation personalities. The meeting
with AMCLOCK/1 was. necessarily brief, and thus the results
are not as extensive as those forwarded by the two circrenced
dispatches (from a 6 October meeting with AMCLOCK/1).
2. A copy of each of the memoranda has been passed by
FIGALAN to the local. LNERGO Cuban Squad, per our existing
informal arrangement. "ELGIN" is the code name for AMCLOCK/1
as used between the Base and LNERGO hore.
3. Items should be extracted for the appropriate 201 files
Howard G. FIGALAN
Attachments:
As stated above

Orig. & 12 Chief, WH/COG, w/atts.

20201-3437.
P.10.10.10 214n. Thin. Sceratory. ELCIN stated that
20201-3437 to spend much of mis time with Loina
Sosfina ANCA Alonso of the Cuban UNGA Delegation. ELCIN
sidi that PANERO scens to have the approval of the DGI
Center here for his modish dress and his excursions to
Greenwich Village, or al. ELCIN assumed that PINERC is
noted to be a very good choice to you around town at night
meeting new people in the house. The first time of the
Apparently PINERO's garb at times approaches that of a hippie.

ACTION REPEAS

Extract for appropriate 201 files
1. Attached herewith for C/WI/COG and COS/WI/MIAMI
are two copies each of two monoranda concerning results
of a 6 October 1969 debriefing of AMCLOCK 1 by Howard G.
FIGALAN on Cuban UN Mission and UNGA Delegation personalities.
2. A copy of each of the two monoranda has been passed
by FIGALAN to the local NERGO Cuban Squad, por our existing
informal agreement. "ELGIN" is the code name for AMCLOCK/1
as used between the Bsc and NERGO here.
3. Results of the 6 October meeting concerning Marta
JANNEZ Martihez (201-784065) of the Cuban Delegation have
been forwarded to above addressees by separate dispatch.
4. The writer anticipates that further and more detailed
debriefing information on personalities of local interest to
this Base and NERGO will be forthcoming in future sessions
with AMCLOCK/1.
5. Items should be extracted for the appropriate 201
files.
Howard G. PIGALAN

RES: DO BASE/NEW YORK 5174
1. As indicated in the reference, the undersigned met with
Subject on 19 October 1965 for the purpose of debriefing him on
items of local interest to the Base and INERGO.
2. Attached herewith is the information obtained at that
meeting, bioken down on separate sheets by major topics:
A) Cuban UN Missicn (CMUN) personnel;
B) Cuban personalities of local interest (but who are
not now in New York);
C) Physical lay-out of the CMUN;
D) Miscellaneous information on the official Cuban
community;
E) Cuban Delegation to the 23rd UNGA.
3. Perhaps the most interesting items are the following:
A) Orlando PRENDES Gutierrez (201-
be the new chief of the DGI contingent within the
CMUN, with Alberto BOZA Hidalgo-Gato (201-331832)
probably serving as the deputy; Jose Raul VIERA
Linares (201-322953). and Jesus JIMENEZ Escobar
(201-749244) follow as the third and fourth ranking
DGI officers;

PUNNANDEZ COSIO Rondinone Director of International

for 14/5 years. Source said that FERNANDEZ COSIO is
a "longer" and a "good" group of the United States. The
system work, for him but is not iccologically oriented. He
is a "loner", and his only real friend is the head of
Directorate of Socialist Countries of the Cuban Foreign
Ministry, who once saved the life of FERNANDEZ COSIO during
BATISTA days. Source terms FERNANDEZ COSIO a superficial
process, which is a "good" group of interested in living
in the family and having money to spend.
2.
Fernandie NAVARZ Plant, 1971, is a first pro-Communist and not really pro-
CASTRO. A political rationalizer who is happy with the regime
that allows him to lead his own life. Would not consider
defection unless the regime changed its attitude toward him,
which is nigh likely, according to Source.
3.
Jose Antonio BABAZA VESNIEZ. BARBAZA is, in Source's belief, a
homosexual (consistent with other reporting on RABAZA). He
works in International Organizations of the Foreign Ministry
under Morta JIMENEZ Martinez, Deputy Chief. While in New York,
the American Association of the United States, he is a member
local Prensa Latins office. Source believes that VILLACORTA
at least has tendencies toward homosexuality himself.
is very close to Osmeni CIENTIUEGOS in Cuba, and the latter has
been the most important Ministry (Other reporting has
indicated that RABAZA is a very strong source of the people
regime after an assignment in Rome; he spent close to a year
in prison). According to Source, CIENTUEGOS spoke up for
RABAZA and this is why he still is in the Foreign Ministry.
He is a member of the National Association of the Delegation or in
the CMRN; he spends little time in the UN Development of the
contrary to others in the Delegation. Source characterized
his behavior as "mysterious", and suspects that RABAZA may be
practicing his sexual proclivities here. He is well-educated
and speaks several languages. He considers himself to be a
good poet.

ACTION REQUIRED: FYI
SEP 28 1980
DOC. MICRC. GER.
The following is a current listing (as of 13 September 1968) of the
officers-Gassigned PCS to the Cuban Permanent Mission to the United Nations
(CMUN) in New York City; Intelligence or security affiliation is also shown
where applicable, The listing is in the probable order of real (as opposed
to UN listing) precedence. As can be seen, the CMUN continues to upgrade
both legitimate diplomatic personnel and intelligence/security personnel both
in terms of quantit) as well as quality.
A. Ricardo LARCON Quesada (201-347590), Ambassador and
Permanent Reprotonatives;
B. Jose Raul JERA Linares (201-328953), Counsellor, DGI
officer;
C. Jesus JIMENEZ Escobar (201-749244), Counsellor, DGI
officer;
D. Antonio DE SOUZA Carvajal (201-354048), Advisor (essentially
a figure-head/without substantive responsibilities or power);
E. Alberto POZA Hidalgo-Gato (201-331832), First Secretary,
DGI officer;
JUL 320002
F. Orlando RRENDED Gutierrez (201-? ), First Secretary,
DGI officer (presulce not confirmed as of 13 September, but was
scheduled to arrive 10 September);

DGI officer;

O. Rolando CONDE Figuoredo (201-354057), Attache;
201-326757
P. Rolando PEREZ Alfonso (201-? ), Attache, (here according
to UN records but not confirmed by LNERGO as of 4 September).
2. In recent months visas have been requested for the following officers,
but they have not arrived as yet, and presumably some of them may not now be
coming for one reason or another.
A. Jorge BOLANOS Suarez (201-787157), Counsellor-designate,
was due to arrive in late August but presence has not been confirmed;
B. Rogclio-RODRIGUEZ Lopez: (201-332665), First Secretary-
designate, DGI officer, visa requested in April 1968 with no further
information available as to whether he will come (presumably he will
not);
C. Cecilia ANDRE Sardain (201-? ), Second Secretary-
designate, same ETA status as Rogclio RODRIGUEZ above.
3. VIERA Linares serves as Charge d'Affaires in the absence of
Ambassador ALARCON Quesada. Up to this point, neither the Base nor LNERGO
have been able to state evidently as to whether VIERA or JIMENEZ Escobar
is the successor to Chafik Homero SAKER Zenni (left PCS October 1967) as the
DGI Station Chief. We both, however, tend to regard JIMENEZ as carrying the
work of the DGI and the National activity and in terms of effectiveness. Now,
with the arrival of BOZA Hidalgo-Cato (who reportedly has been the deputy to
Ramon OROZA Naveran, he has been of U.S. operations for the DGI, per our last
information), it remains to be seen if BOZA figures higher in the local hierarchy
than VIERA or JIMENEZ. With JIMENEZ, VIERA, BOZA, and PRENDES
Gutierrez, the local DGI stations has more ranking talent than has been the norm,
The Cubans do not necessarily do their intelligence officers in Mission titles
equivalent to their true ranks and responsibilities.

CONINUATION OF

DISPATCH
4. In terms of culncrability from the INLIAPE standpoint, the
intelligence/security personnel at this point appear to offer little in the
way of approach potential. Jorge POLANOS Suarez (if he. cosues) and
Gustave Adolfo PLAZA Petersen, on the basis of known information,
seem the likeliest targets for us is of now. Both the Base and LNERGO,
however, continue to look at all of them in this regard.
5. It will be noted from the above that of the 16 CMUN personnel
now here, 8 are identified DGI/DSE, 2 are presumed DGI, and 1 (GELABERT)
may be DSE or DIER. The percentage of personnel involved with intelligence/
security thus ranges from a minimum of 50% up to 69% of the total CMUN
personnel strength.
6. The number of official Cubans in New York will, of course, be
swelled by the arrival of the Cuban Delegation to the 23rd UN General
Assembly this month. We have requested, via DO BASE/NEW YORK 4844,
traces on the 8 of the 12 man delegation on whom we hold no information.
Howard G. FIGALAN

3 August 1965
MENCRANDUN FOB:
FROH:
SUBJECT:
Owner of Auto Bearing Califorais License HEW 810
(How: MEXICAN: Diplomatic Plates D-136)
1. Reference is under to your memorandum of 26 July 1965 on the above
subject. This office had no objection to your including information cos-
tained in our memorandum of 6 April 1965 in a report to the Bureau of
International Commerce, The Bureau of Customs, and the Immigration and
Noturalization Service.
2. It is noted that according to a usually reliable source, this
automobile is currently registered to Canilo Dommeach Gadea, who was
Commercial Counselor of the Cuban Embassy until he left for Cuba on
10 February 1965. As of the present date, the automobile is still being
used by the Cuban Embassy.
Distribution: Legal Attache
THIS INFORMAT ON IS FROM A CONFIDENTIAL SOURCE. IT MUST NOT BE DISSEMINATED
IN WHOLE OR IN PART OUTSIDE YOUR OFFICE WITHOUT PRIOR APPROVAL OF THE
ORICINATING OFFICE IN MEXICO CITY.

memorandum is now in possession of an employee of the
Cuban Embassy, which could be a violation of export laws
and regulations. Your approval is therefore requested to
include this information in your memorandum in a report
to the Bureau of International Commerce, The Bureau of
Customs, and Immigration and Naturalization Service.

Chief of Station, San Jose

Chief, WH Division
Chief of Station, Kexico City
PIBUPMEN/Unknown Costa Rican in Contact with Cuban Embassy
Action Required: For information, and see paragraph two.
1. According to LIEWOWY, on 23 April 1965, an unidentified man
called the Cuban Embassy in Mexico City to speak to the Ambassador,
who was not in. The man refused to give his name but said he was the
person who used to be seen with "the young blond man" from the Embassy,
Subject asked the Embassy secretary to tell the Ambassador that he had
been the most important, but he was a nice shoe to Kexico from Costa
Rica and that has he was here, but could be the most important, but he was said
that he had seen the Ambassador frequently but had been to:1 not to use
names on the telephone; that he had received the caule at the beginning of
Boly Week but could not get a plane reservation them; that they had known
the message, but he was the most important, but he was the most important
man and now gone to Cuba, subject was the most important, but the
of the person who had taken the young's Place; and that the cable had
alluded to some business they were going to take care of. Finally, Subject
said to tell the Ambassador that he was the doctor friend of Manuel.
2. The Station is unable to identify Subject. However, the Blind man
is probably Rogelio Rodriguez Lopez; Second Secretary and identified Cuban
intelligence officer, who left PES for Cuba on 5 March 1965. The Station
would be interested to know the identity of Subject if it can be determined
by the San Jose Station.
Willard C. CURTIS

MERCARDUM FOR:
FROM:
SUBJECT:
Owner of Auto Bearing California License NEW 810
1. Reference is made to your concentration of 26 harch 1965 on
the above subject. According to a usually reliable source, the
automobile which previously bore California License NEW 810, now
had Mexican diplomatio plates D-136 and is owned by the Cuban
Embassy in Mexico City. The date on which the license plates were
changed is not known.
2. The description of Rogelio Rodrigues, who purchased the
autcouble in California, does not fit the description? Rogelio
Rodriguez Lopez, who was a member of the staff of use Cuban Embassy
in Mexico City at the time of the purchase; and the identity of the
purchaser is unknown.

Date : March 26, 1965
To
:
From 118
Subject: UNKNOWN SUBJECT; Owner of Auto
Bearing California License HEW 810
This document is as the uss of you
record
concer
It has been reliably reported to this office that
captioned vehicle, not otherwise described, was observed on
the grounds of the Cuban Embassy in Mexico City at 1130 A.M.
on October 29, 1964.
The investigation of date to 1120 identify the owner has
developed that the proposed vehicle's MAA 1961 Ford Falcon two-
door with Vehicle Identification Number 1R11S123981,
Investigation in California has disclosed the captioned
vehicle was last sold to one ROGELIO RODRIGUEZ gave a
false address in the Los Angeles area to the seller of the
vehicle. At the time of the sale, RODRIGUEZ indicated that
the was buying the automobile for someone else in Mexico, and
would allegedly go to Mexico in the automobile.
RODRIGUEZ was described at the time of the purchase
of the vehicle as a man between 35 and 40 years of age,
apparent a Mayoican (guidging from his Spanish, dress, etc.)
and was allegedly staying with relatives in Los Angeles,
California,
CONFIDENTIAL
John

Downgrading and Declassification

Comrede Ferr
Several days ago we received a request from comrade Nulogio with reference
to your need of a loan to pay some debts, which resulted from recent purchases
made by you.
We are aware that your hark requires certain commodities, such as a
presentable house, capable of making persons, who you receive, feel comfortable
in the atmosphere they are in.
How, you should have an equalized your comodic possibilities before incurring
those of the following items to you would leave realized that these were not
within your reach (h. 105), for which reason you would have turned to us, with
the purpose of finding a solution to that problem.
We are instructing comrade Eulogio to make you a reasonable loan with
which you can get out of your present debts.
In the future you should consult us and in particular present a plan to
corrade Eulogio, you any problem of that nature, with the confidence that it
will be solved.
You should make us a report justifying the loan that you will get to
pay the debts you have."
John H. CORNISH

MEMORANDUM FOR:
SUBJECT
In 8/8 communications, the agent is given a name, separate
from his own pseudogym, as an indicator. in the fumos operation,
the use of the name "JULIO" meant that the lettor was for "DUUARDO"
that is Rogello RODRICUEZ, who had that as one of his pseudogyma
and used it in August 1962 when he was in the MA Section at
DGI (Cuban intelligence service) Headquarters. The Valladares
Operation similarly used "GENAIRO" to indicate that the letter was
for "TEDOTOR," identity unknown, but a case officer in MA
Section in August 1962.
